# Changelog

All notable changes to this repository are recorded in this file as lead-paragraph summaries. Detailed maintainer-level entries (full Added / Changed / Removed / Fixed / Security / Verification sections per change) are kept in [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md). This is how this project's maintainer tracks the full audit trail. The convention is project-specific; forks may delete `.working/` and adopt their own approach to detailed change tracking. The mechanics are documented in the [`change-tracking` governance rule](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/change-tracking.md).

The format follows [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/) loosely; individual document versions follow semantic versioning as defined in [`specification-ingestion.md`](specification-ingestion.md). The library as a whole carries a Calendar Versioning (CalVer) version of the form `YYYY.MM.patch`; see [`specification-master-project.md`](specification-master-project.md) section 4.5.

## 2026-07-02, Library Version 2026.07.76, PR #588

The maintainer-pre-authorized COBIT fit-pass recodes ship: the cross-framework matrix's three risk rows move to their fit-verified controls ([`governance/matrix-cross-framework-alignment.md`](governance/matrix-cross-framework-alignment.md) 1.1.10: EDM03 Ensured Risk Optimization, APO12.02 Analyze risk, and EDM03.01 Evaluate risk management with the appetite row's ISO 31000 cell re-pointed to Clause 6.3.4 Defining risk criteria), the exception policy's three APO12.03 carriers move together to APO12.02 ([`governance/policy-exception-and-risk-acceptance-management.md`](governance/policy-exception-and-risk-acceptance-management.md) 1.3.10), and the four BAI05.02 supplier carriers move together to APO10.05 Monitor vendor performance and compliance ([`supply-chain/procedure-supplier-audit.md`](supply-chain/procedure-supplier-audit.md) 1.0.9, [`compliance/policy-compliance-and-audit-management.md`](compliance/policy-compliance-and-audit-management.md) 1.0.10). The #587 verifier's ISO 31000 clause-number correction lands on its three carriers (6.7 to 6.6, Monitoring and review; [`governance/procedure-grc-programme-management-and-annual-review.md`](governance/procedure-grc-programme-management-and-annual-review.md) 1.0.6, [`governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md`](governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md) 1.27.54), and all four mis-titled MEA01 cells in the compliance-management table are restored to their canonical practice titles (the routed two plus the two the #587 post-merge sweep's whole-table check surfaced), with the verifier-caught MEA01 objective-title suffix corrected on its two carriers ([`governance/policy-exception-and-risk-acceptance-management.md`](governance/policy-exception-and-risk-acceptance-management.md) 1.3.11, [`governance/template-library-health-report.md`](governance/template-library-health-report.md) 1.0.6). The canonical MEA01.05 title carries a bare imperative the `ensure that` rule flags, so [`tools/lint-language.py`](tools/lint-language.py) gains a narrow verbatim-external-title span mask (two fixtures, suite 284 to 286; [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) 1.16.39). Every replacement code and title was re-verified against the held COBIT extract at apply time, applied by a count-guarded deterministic script with a zero-residual re-parse. Batches the #587 [`/validate-pr`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) and [`/retro`](.working/improvement-log.md) rows with five in-window sweep fixes. Library 2026.07.75 to 2026.07.76; README 1.9.436 to 1.9.437.

## 2026-07-02, Library Version 2026.07.70, PR #582

Tooling (the GR-P3 graduation, census-first design): **the partial-rewrite tension-marker check ships as the advisory aid [`tools/tension-scan.py`](tools/tension-scan.py), not a standing gate.** For a commit range, the aid pairs each rewritten TODO bullet, ledger table row, bold-led paragraph, or plain paragraph line (an added line sharing ANY pairing key, the bold lead token, the first two table cells, or a normalized prefix, with a removed line in the same file, so an edit inside one key region still pairs) and flags any whose new text carries a status-claim token (e.g. CONFIRMED, CLOSED, RESOLVED, shipped) alongside a hedge token (e.g. NEEDS-UPSTREAM, pending, TBD, awaiting), printing each untruncated for an end-to-end read; it always exits 0 on findings (2 only on usage or git error), and its docstring discloses the known recall limit (a rewrite editing a block's opening words with no stable lead or cells escapes pairing; a clean run means nothing detected, not nothing rewritten). The aid-not-gate shape is census-driven: a build-time census over [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) and the six working ledgers found 91 legitimate block-level status+hedge coincidences (honest narrative and bullets quoting the marker vocabulary), so the bookkeeping-gate family's zero-false-positive bar is unreachable and the contradiction judgment stays human; logged as a proceeded default and **CONFIRMED by the maintainer at their 2026-07-02 return round** (the same round redirected the gate-60 threshold to fail-at-3, authorized the CLAUDE.md batch, and decided the lifecycle-vocabulary, coverage-batch-2, and coverage-vocabulary calls; each recorded against its queue item). Exercised on a historical five-merge range (7 rewritten blocks paired at the final detection logic, 2 legitimate candidates flagged) and a synthetic contradiction (the #563-class archetype, flagged) before shipping; the first historical probe and the pre-push verifier each exposed and fixed a detection gap (bold-led ledger paragraphs invisible to the initial block pattern; single-key pairing broken by an edit inside the bold lead itself). Also dispositions the five #581 sweep findings: the record-drift cluster fixed in-window (the root and mirror #581 leads reconciled to eleven cells across twelve re-grade events with Kubernetes at Partial, corrections noted inline; the DONE entry rewritten, a drift the orchestrator had independently caught pre-sweep; the handoff refreshed) and the second coverage-gaps triage batch routed to [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) section 3.14 with every claim re-verified at file. ## 2026-07-02, Library Version 2026.07.63, PR #575

Tooling (the QA-and-guardrails step's first build, escalated by the #573 retro): **the GR-12 post-fix residual-scan aid ships as [`tools/residual-scan.py`](tools/residual-scan.py)**. Given a corrected token, the aid scans every text surface in the working tree (no git-tracked filter, so untracked files are covered too; never an enumerated input set, the completion-verification lesson), prints every hit as an untruncated full line (the read-before-triage lesson from Sweep 82), labels each LIVE / LEDGER / FROZEN-RECORD, suppresses the frozen per-run archives by default, and exits non-zero on any LIVE hit so it chains as a completion check after a fix. It is an aid like the CHANGELOG preflight, not a numbered gate (its token vocabulary is per-fix, so it cannot run unattended in CI); the authoritative gates are unchanged. Shipped now because the fix-named-carrier-miss-the-sibling shape recurred five times across the #571 to #574 window (each caught in-window by a verifier or sweep), satisfying the GR-P3 prioritization bar. ## 2026-07-01, Library Version 2026.07.9, PR #521

Word-form collection-count detection in gate 39 (TODO §1.3-B, closing §1.3) for local project: broadened [`tools/lint-gate-count-consistency.py`](tools/lint-gate-count-consistency.py) with a word-to-number map (1 to 99) and four narrow, anchored word-form patterns (P9 to P12) on top of its existing digit gate-count patterns, closing the gate-39-blind word-form class that let a stale "fifty-seven" survive in the guardrail-review growth narrative until #510 corrected it by hand. The new patterns detect word-form gate counts (a qualified "<word> audit gates" and "<word>-gate"), the qualified governance-rule count ("<word> governance rules", sourced like gate 41 from the rule-file directory), and the growth-narrative "rules/skills/gates to <word>" shape (the collection keyword selects which canonical count is checked, and this is the only skill-count check). The design is precision-first and maintainer-chosen (over full coverage or won't-fix): the pervasive bare small-word-number prose ("one gate, one concern", "two rules overlap", "Six rules", "the two skills run as a suite") is never matched, because no bare "<word> rules/skills/gates" pattern exists, only the qualified and growth-narrative shapes; and a "## Version history" section is skipped as a frozen change log (the in-document analogue of the existing CHANGELOG.md file exemption), since its rows legitimately quote superseded counts. ## 2026-06-30, Library Version 2026.06.487, PR #509

Per-document ISO/IEC 27001:2022 Annex A validity audit (gate 58, closing TODO §1.2) for local project: adds [`tools/lint-document-iso-annex-a.py`](tools/lint-document-iso-annex-a.py), the ISO-column sibling of gate 54 (per-document NIST CSF 2.0) and the per-document counterpart of gate 49 (which validates the central matrix's ISO column). It validates ISO/IEC 27001:2022 Annex A control codes and management-system clause references wherever they appear in any corpus document's framework-reference or crosswalk tables, catching a non-existent Annex A control (`A.8.99`), a non-2022 theme (`A.9.2`, a 2013-edition code), an out-of-range or inverted range, or an out-of-range clause (`§12`). The design is precision-first and maintainer-approved (separate gate rather than folding into gate 54; theme-only references such as `A.5` accepted as valid): validation fires only inside a cell governed by an explicit `ISO/IEC 27001:2022` label (edition-pinned, so a `:2013` table is not mis-validated) and is table-scoped, so a bare `§6` in document prose, almost always the document's OWN section 6, is never read as an ISO clause. It recognizes single codes, theme-only refs, same-theme ranges (`A.8.20 to A.8.21`), clauses, and comma/semicolon lists, in both the framework-as-column and framework-as-row table shapes, excluding the central matrix (gate 49's target) and the `dev-security/claude-rules/` pack subtree. The shared structural facts (Annex A theme counts A.5-A.8 = 37/8/14/34 = 93; clauses §4-§10) and the `check_iso_token` single-token validator were extracted into a new [`tools/iso_27001_reference.py`](tools/iso_27001_reference.py) module (mirroring [`tools/nist_csf_reference.py`](tools/nist_csf_reference.py)); gate 49's linter was refactored to import from it so the two ISO gates cannot drift. Wired across all four audit-programme surfaces (workflow, runner, pre-commit, [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) §6 table + §6 detailed prose + §5 grouped list) with a 9-test regression fixture in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py). Substantive new-gate change verified by a pre-push skeptical verifier; all 58 gates pass (gate 35 confirms four-surface parity at 58; gate 39 confirms count consistency at 58 across 469 files; gate 58 clean over 318 corpus documents). Closes TODO §1.2 (rotated to [`.working/DONE.md`](.working/DONE.md); P1 4 items). Also batches the #508 [`/validate-pr`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) (0 findings) and [`/retro`](.working/improvement-log.md) rows, the IEEE-2883-ingestion bookkeeping, and the handoff refresh, committed on the branch. Library 2026.06.486 to 2026.06.487; README 1.9.357 to 1.9.358.

## 2026-06-30, Library Version 2026.06.486, PR #508

NIST SP 800-88 Rev. 2 re-point and IEEE 2883 introduction (§1.5 version-upgrade follow-up #3, the last) for local project: NIST SP 800-88 Rev. 2 (final 2025-09-26; Rev. 1 withdrawn the same day) substantively reframed media sanitization around an enterprise programme and, apart from cryptographic erase, replaced the hands-on technique detail with a deferral to IEEE 2883, NSA specifications, or an organizationally-approved standard. ## 2026-06-30, Library Version 2026.06.482, PR #504

Governance-pack change for local project: codified the project-local **compute-don't-ask** convention (#269, the open §1.3 residual) into the [`clarify-before-acting`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/clarify-before-acting.md) pack rule as a **compute-first gate**. Before surfacing any question, the assistant now applies one prior test, is the answer a findable fact it can retrieve itself (a file location, a citation, a count, a version, where a term is used in the corpus, what a document currently says)? When findable, it runs the `grep` or read and surfaces the answer, never the raw question; the rule's existing ask-vs-default test now governs only the genuine ambiguities and authorial choices that survive the gate. The gate is named the action-side companion to [`validate-inference-before-action`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/validate-inference-before-action.md), a paired `Asking for a findable fact` anti-pattern was added, the byte-identical [`.claude/` mirror](.claude/rules/governance/clarify-before-acting.md) was updated in lock-step, and the paired [`clarify-before-acting` skill](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/clarify-before-acting/SKILL.md) gained the compute-first step plus a Red Flag for parity. Maintainer-prompted after a session asked the maintainer to locate two citations a corpus `grep` would have found. Batches the #503 [`/validate-pr`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) and [`/retro`](.working/improvement-log.md) rows and the surfaced [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) §3.14 item committed on the branch. No corpus document body touched. Pack 1.53.6 to 1.53.7; Library 2026.06.481 to 2026.06.482; README 1.9.352 to 1.9.353.

## 2026-06-30, Library Version 2026.06.479, PR #501

D5 rotation-check broadening + CLAUDE.md backlog-item-keyed reword (P1: §1.3 rotation-prevention, the #495/#496 miss). Broadened the D5 PR-time backlog-rotation check ([`tools/check-todo-rotation-on-pr.py`](tools/check-todo-rotation-on-pr.py)) so it detects three closure-assertion forms, not only the old `clos... TODO §`: it now also fires on the `FR-N CLOSED` major-closure marker and the prose-named `clos... the ... (backlog item | TODO item | directive)` form (the shape of the #495 miss, where a prose-named "OT post-ingestion validation" item was closed without rotation, invisible to the section-only trigger). The three forms were chosen empirically for false-positive-freedom: each was tested against the entire CHANGELOG history (root + detailed, ~14k lines) and matched only genuine current-PR closures. A bare lowercase `Closes FR-N` is deliberately NOT a trigger (it matched ~95 lines including past-closure narration such as "PR #143 closed FR-9", which would false-fail a standing gate); the close-out-checklist convention covers that residual (maintainer decision). Added positive and negative regression fixtures to [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py) and updated the §6.1 D5 prose in [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md). Reworded the [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) rotation lines (PR-workflow step 7 and the close-out checklist) to be backlog-item-keyed, not FR/§-keyed (maintainer-approved): a prose-named or maintainer-directed item is a TODO item that rotates like any other. Rotated the §1.3 rotation-prevention sub-item to [`.working/DONE.md`](.working/DONE.md) (the rest of §1.3 stays open) and tidied the doubled `---` separators the #500 renumber left. Batches the #500 [`/validate-pr`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) (0 findings) and [`/retro`](.working/improvement-log.md) rows. Library 2026.06.478 to 2026.06.479; README 1.9.349 to 1.9.350.

## 2026-06-30, Library Version 2026.06.464, PR #486

FR-73 for local project: split AI ethics review out of the [AI Governance Council](ai/charter-ai-governance-council.md) into a new independent [`ai/charter-ai-ethics-review-panel.md`](ai/charter-ai-ethics-review-panel.md) (AI Ethics Review Panel Charter, v1.0.0), closing FR-73 (the AIGC collapsed ethics into the same body that does risk and compliance, with no separate ethics panel or independent challenge mechanism). The new charter establishes a panel structurally independent of the AIGC (its chair and a voting majority are not AIGC voting members; it is owned by the Chief Risk Officer and reports to the CRO and the Board, outside the AIGC's reporting line to the Enterprise Risk Committee) and gives it a documented five-step independent challenge mechanism: the Panel can challenge an AIGC decision on ethical grounds, the AIGC must reconsider and respond in writing, a challenged irreversible action is held pending the response, and an unresolved objection escalates to the Board above the AIGC. The Panel is a challenge-and-escalation body, not a veto (deployment approval stays with the AIGC). Edited the AIGC charter ([`ai/charter-ai-governance-council.md`](ai/charter-ai-governance-council.md), 1.2.2 to 1.2.3) to cede independent ethical review to the Panel, add the reconsider-and-respond obligation, and reference the Panel throughout (removing the AIGC's residual self-claim to perform independent ethics review). Listed in [`ai/README.md`](ai/README.md) and [`governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md`](governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md); generated artefacts regenerated. Authored via the high-assurance harness: the false-negative (completeness/independence) verifier found zero gaps (independence structural rather than asserted; the challenge mechanism reaches above the AIGC; the split is complete on the AIGC side) and the false-positive (citation/authority/contradiction) verifier found zero defects (all four frameworks registered; the Panel correctly bounded as challenge-not-veto; new seats hedged as adopter-mapped; reporting lines consistent and non-circular). Batches the #485 [`/validate-pr`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) (0 findings) and the #485 QA rows. Library 2026.06.463 to 2026.06.464; README 1.9.334 to 1.9.335.

## 2026-06-29, Library Version 2026.06.447, PR #469

Adds the **D5 PR-time backlog-rotation check** (the workflow step "Backlog-rotation-on-PR check", [`tools/check-todo-rotation-on-pr.py`](tools/check-todo-rotation-on-pr.py)), the PR-time complementary half of the §4.10 TODO/DONE-rotation bookkeeping-parity gate family, **closing TODO §4.10** (the static content-side half, gate 57, shipped in #468). The check scans a PR's ADDED [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md) and [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) lines for an assertion that the PR closes a backlog item (the `clos...`-then-`TODO §` adjacency), and when one is present it requires the same diff to rotate the item by touching BOTH [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) and [`.working/DONE.md`](.working/DONE.md); a `TodoRotation:` CHANGELOG trailer opts out (a narration-only mention or a multi-PR closure), and a session-closing handoff PR is exempt. It catches the wholesale-forgotten rotation that gate 57 cannot see (the #466 class: [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) never edited, so nothing self-marked for gate 57 to detect), the coverage gap the #466 `/retro` surfaced. Like D1 to D4 it is a PR-only delta check, not a numbered gate: it runs only in [`tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh`](tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh) and the [`quality.yml`](.github/workflows/quality.yml) `pull_request` section, is documented as row D5 in [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) §6.1, and is exempt from the gate-name parity audit; the gate count is unchanged at 57. A 2-case fixture is added to [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py). This PR dogfoods the check: its own CHANGELOG asserts a backlog closure, so the §4.10 rotation (deleted from [`TODO.md`](TODO.md), added to [`.working/DONE.md`](.working/DONE.md)) is what makes D5 pass on this very diff. Batches the #468 [`/validate-pr`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. ## 2026-06-29, Library Version 2026.06.439, PR #461

`.claude/` + `.working/` + pack for local project: codifies the **skeptical pre-push verification** standard (maintainer-directed: "make consistent use of skeptical verifier subagents a standard for anything other than a quick fix"). A new unnumbered section in [`dev-security/claude-rules/governance/ai-assistant-workflow-disciplines.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/ai-assistant-workflow-disciplines.md) (mirrored byte-identical to [`.claude/rules/governance/ai-assistant-workflow-disciplines.md`](.claude/rules/governance/ai-assistant-workflow-disciplines.md)) states a tiered standard layered on the five disciplines (NOT a sixth, so the "five disciplines" framing is unchanged): no standing verifier for quick-fix / bookkeeping changes; ONE refute-briefed verifier subagent pre-push for substantive changes; the full [`high-assurance-verification`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/high-assurance-verification.md) harness for sensitive changes. It encodes the validate-then-fix-then-re-verify finding loop (a verifier finding is a hypothesis until validated; three-iteration cap, then defer to maintainer review) and the "overruling a verifier is never silent" discipline (log the finding verbatim, the overruling reasoning, and the exact revert path; an unattended override is surfaced at the next attended boundary). The project operationalization is a new override register [`.working/verifier-overrides.md`](.working/verifier-overrides.md) (pending / reviewed states, maintainer-cleared like a pending decision) plus `/resume` step-7 surfacing in [`.claude/commands/resume.md`](.claude/commands/resume.md) and a note in [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md)'s attended-autonomous section and rule index. The "stricter early-run oversight of the verifier" the maintainer asked for is deliberately kept in memory, NOT codified, so it need not be unwound later. Pack `1.53.1` to `1.53.2`. Batches the #460 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. No corpus-document body change. Library `2026.06.438` to `2026.06.439`; README `1.9.309` to `1.9.310`.

The assistant may *offer* a handoff for the maintainer to consider before substantial/critical/long work, as a non-default suggestion. The unchanged downstream parts of the section (the per-PR likelihood assessment, the named options A-D, the timeout) were reconciled so none still treats work-shape as a wind-down justification. ## 2026-06-29, Library Version 2026.06.431, PR #453

Pack-skill addition (distributable pack content): added the seventeenth skill, [`dev-security/claude-rules/skills/high-assurance-verification/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/high-assurance-verification/SKILL.md) (slash command `/high-assurance`), the executable companion to the twelfth governance rule shipped in #450. The rule states the discipline (when and why a sensitive change, gate-blind on correctness, delicate at scale, costly to get wrong, warrants the heavier pre-apply harness); this skill states the procedure (how), as a seven-step process that operationalizes the rule's five-stage harness: confirm the three-condition trigger and open the persistent-register row, research fan-out, a mechanical signal pass over the negatives (open-on-negative-with-signal), two independent adversarial verifiers (false-negative and false-positive lenses, blind to each other and to the research), a programmatic invariant floor, a deterministic scripted apply plus re-parse, and close the register row and surface. It follows the pack's eight-section skill template and `derives_from` [`high-assurance-verification.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/high-assurance-verification.md). Wired: the new slash command [`.claude/commands/high-assurance.md`](.claude/commands/high-assurance.md) with step-identifier parity (steps 1-7, gate 44); the [`tools/lint-paired-skill-step-parity.py`](tools/lint-paired-skill-step-parity.py) PAIRS registry (now 8 pairs); the pack [`README.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) skills tree (gate 41, 16 to 17 skills) and version-history row; the [`skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) growth-narrative count "sixteen" to "seventeen" (gate-39-blind word-form). ## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.428, PR #450

Add the twelfth governance pack rule, [`high-assurance-verification.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/high-assurance-verification.md), standardizing the independent-adversarial-verification method that the #448 CSA AICM v1.1 matrix column was built with (maintainer-requested). The rule defines a heavier pre-apply harness for *sensitive* changes (those that are gate-blind on correctness, delicate at scale, and costly to get wrong): research fan-out, a mechanical signal pass over the negatives, two independent adversarial verifiers (a false-negative lens and a false-positive lens, blind to each other and to the research), a programmatic invariant floor, and a deterministic scripted apply plus a re-parse, so apply-correctness does not rest on the orchestrator's in-context precision. It is the proactive counterpart to [`trust-recovery-escalation.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/trust-recovery-escalation.md) (reactive) and a heavier tier above the routine [`ai-assistant-workflow-disciplines.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/ai-assistant-workflow-disciplines.md) research-assistant flow. Sensitive items persist across sessions in a new register, [`.working/high-assurance/register.md`](.working/high-assurance/register.md), surfaced at `/resume`, so the harness recurs to completion across session boundaries; the register is seeded with the #448 AICM column as its inaugural `verified` exemplar. ## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.420, PR #442

Pack-guidance addition (distributable pack content): added [`dev-security/claude-rules/guidance-claude-md-optimization.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/guidance-claude-md-optimization.md), a maintainer-facing guidance doc on the keep-and-condense method for an always-loaded rules file. It documents the keep-or-cut taxonomy (keep actionable rules, procedure steps, commands, concrete values, boundaries, and source pointers; cut rationale, war-stories, provenance, and duplication), the removal-ledger discipline (every cut recorded verbatim with its expected gain, its risk, and the falsification signal that would mean restore it, reviewed on a cadence), and the verification that targets the one failure that matters (a dropped actionable rule: an actionable-token survival check plus a section-by-section old-versus-new walk). It is the distillation of the method this library used on its own [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) in PR #441. It is a pack-root doc alongside [`setup-generator-prompt.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/setup-generator-prompt.md), not a governance rule, and is not mirrored into the local rules copies. Wired into the pack [`README.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) directory tree and version history (pack `1.51.1` to `1.51.2`), and adds [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) §4.28 (the low-priority narrow diagnostic skill the guidance doc's judgment-heavy core cannot be mechanized into). Batches the #441 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.419` to `2026.06.420`; README `1.9.290` to `1.9.291`.

## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.418, PR #440

Hot-fix (assistant-workflow tooling; invisible to adopters): fixed a HIGH correctness bug in [`tools/pre-push-guard.sh`](tools/pre-push-guard.sh) that the #439 `/validate-pr` caught. The guard captured `rc=$?` immediately after `if ! tools/run_all_audits.sh; then`, which captures the NEGATED status (0) rather than the runner's real exit code, so the guard exited 0 even when a runner FAILED, letting `tools/pre-push-guard.sh && git push` proceed despite a failed gate (the guard did not actually guard on its failure path). Fixed by capturing `$?` from the bare command (`tools/run_all_audits.sh; rc=$?; if [ "${rc}" -ne 0 ]; then ...`) on both runner blocks; the failure path is now tested explicitly (a faithful guard copy with a failing runner exits non-zero), closing the gap that let the bug ship (the #439 self-test exercised only the both-pass path). Also fixed a LOW finding: the best-effort fetch was hardcoded to `origin main` and ignored a `BASE_REF` override, now `git fetch origin`. Batches the #439 `/validate-pr` (2 in-window findings, 1 HIGH + 1 LOW, both fixed here) and `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.417` to `2026.06.418`; README `1.9.288` to `1.9.289`.

## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.417, PR #439

Assistant-workflow tooling change (invisible to adopters): added [`tools/pre-push-guard.sh`](tools/pre-push-guard.sh), a single pre-push QA gate that chains [`run_all_audits.sh`](tools/run_all_audits.sh) then [`run-pr-time-checks.sh`](tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh) and exits non-zero on the first failure, and wired it into the [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) PR-workflow (steps 1 to 2 now push via `tools/pre-push-guard.sh && git push`). This codifies the maintainer-directed preventative from the #438 retrospective: the momentum-over-verification slip where an "intermediate" push skips the mandatory pre-push runner and a delta gate flips CI red after the fact (the #438 CI-red cycle). Git hooks do not fire in this environment, so an `&&`-chained guard (mirroring the existing [`preflight-changelog.py`](tools/preflight-changelog.py)`&& git commit` commit-gate) is what actually enforces the discipline; CI remains the correctness backstop, the guard removes the fail-then-fix loop. Complements, does not close, the TODO §4.6 QA-cadence gate family (gate 50 catches a missing QA row post-merge; this guard catches the runner-skip pre-push). Batches the #438 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.416` to `2026.06.417`; README `1.9.287` to `1.9.288`.

## 2026-06-28, Library Version 2026.06.401, PR #423

**New governance rule: `surface-counterproductive-instructions` (the eleventh pack rule).** Adds [`dev-security/claude-rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md): a clear instruction is not automatically a correct one, so when executing it as given would reduce efficiency, effectiveness, or productivity, lower quality, destroy work already done, contradict a stated goal, or rest on a stale-state belief, the assistant stops, considers, and surfaces the concern with named options before acting (stop, consider, confirm), with a charitable-interpretation corollary (do not silently take a harmful literal reading; never revert or discard committed work without confirming) and an anti-over-ask calibration (fire only on material downside; one informed round; accept an informed override). Maintainer-directed after a prior session read a "wind down" instruction literally and silently reverted committed in-flight work it did not intend to destroy. Wired across the three gate-41 governance-rule enumeration surfaces (the pack [`README.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) tree plus its "two areas" prose, pack [`CLAUDE.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/CLAUDE.md), and project [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md)), the byte-identical [`.claude/rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md`](.claude/rules/governance/surface-counterproductive-instructions.md) mirror and its [`tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py`](tools/lint-claude-rules-sync.py) MIRROR_MAP entry, and the ten-to-eleven count advance in the [`tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py`](tools/lint-collection-enumeration-consistency.py) docstring and the [`dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) growth narrative. The privacy jurisdiction index ([`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md):137, the "2026 Update summary" bullet) said the Digital Personal Data Protection Rules 2025 were "published February 2025 and entered into force April 2025" with the Data Protection Board "commenced operations", an early-2025 projection that contradicted both [`privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-india.md`](privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-india.md):28 and the canonical [`governance/register-canonical-citations.md`](governance/register-canonical-citations.md):147. Per the finding's own instruction the notification date was **verified against external sources at fix time** (the maintainer authorised attempting this in-session rather than deferring): the final Rules were notified by MeitY via Gazette Notification G.S.R. 846(E) **dated 13 November 2025** (draft published 3 January 2025), with a three-phase commencement (Data Protection Board provisions on notification; consent-manager provisions around November 2026; the remaining substantive obligations around May 2027), confirmed against two independent legal-firm sources. India is the one jurisdiction absent from the scratch `ref/legislation/` base, so external web verification was the only ground-truth path. The index bullet was reconciled to the annex and the citations register (now mutually consistent across all three surfaces); the index's India table row (:118, "DPDPA 2023 / Rules 2025") carried no date claim and was left unchanged, and no parallel stale "April 2025" occurrence exists elsewhere in the corpus. Per-document Version + Date bumped on the one edited doc ([`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md) `1.0.6` to `1.0.7`); [`taxonomy.yml`](taxonomy.yml) and [`docs/maturity-scorecard.md`](docs/maturity-scorecard.md) regenerated. Closes FR-175 (TODO to DONE), clearing the entire High set FR-168..175. Also batches the #415 `/validate-pr` (0 findings, 1 sub-threshold style advisory not routed) and `/retro` rows. ## 2026-06-27, Library Version 2026.06.373, PR #394

Added an advisory semantic-fit triage tool, [`tools/audit-matrix-semantic-fit.py`](tools/audit-matrix-semantic-fit.py), for the gate-blind "valid code, wrong control" class (a control code that exists in its catalogue, so gates 48/49/54 pass it, but is the wrong control for the row's document). The stdlib-only, recall-oriented tool worklists rows in the compliance matrix ([`compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md`](compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md)) and in per-document framework-alignment tables that lack any lexical anchor between the document subject and the cited control titles, narrowing the scope for the queued `/matrix-fit` semantic audit ([`TODO.md`](TODO.md) section 4.20, PR B) to adjudicate. It is deliberately NOT a gate: `audit-`-named so the parity and regression machinery does not auto-discover it, never wired into [`tools/run_all_audits.sh`](tools/run_all_audits.sh) or CI, and it always exits 0 (a lexical signal cannot be precision-first for semantic fit, so its output is a worklist, not a verdict). This is the first half of the cadenced-semantic-fit-audit capability; the `/matrix-fit` skill and its cadence wiring follow in PR B. Also batches the clean Sweep 61 records (the loop-break corpus-wide `/validate` over the #390 to #393 deltas, which independently re-verified #392's control-code remediation against the CSA CCM v4.1 ground truth: 0 error, 0 warning, 2 out-of-window notes). ## 2026-06-27, Library Version 2026.06.370, PR #391

Standards-validation discipline for local project: codify how the scratch repo's `ref/standards/` reference base is validated when it informs corpus work, the discipline whose absence let the CCM/AICM-confusion hole (#390) and a class of worker semantic mislabels go uncaught until a manual cross-check surfaced them. Adds a maintainer dev-aid [`tools/verify-reference-modules.py`](tools/verify-reference-modules.py) that confirms the in-repo control-reference modules (which gates 48/49/54 enforce against) match the authoritative scratch source extracts in both directions: `CCM_V41` against the CSA CCM v4.1.0 catalogue CSV (207 codes), `AICM_V11` against the AICM v1.1.0 catalogue CSV (247 codes), and the NIST CSF 2.0 categories against the CSWP-29 full-text extract (22 categories). It is a dev-aid, not a CI gate (the scratch source is absent in CI), named `verify-*` not `lint-*` so the gate machinery does not auto-discover it, and it skips cleanly when the scratch base is unavailable. Codifies the **standards-validation discipline** in the [`multi-session-orchestration`](.working/multi-session-orchestration.md) runbook section 6: (1) code-set parity via the new aid, (2) validate a mapping's semantic fit against the source control *title*, not the code number (code existence is necessary but not sufficient: a valid code can be the wrong control), (3) CCM and AICM are distinct catalogues, never confuse them. Adds two worker-brief guard rails ([`worker-brief-template.md`](.working/worker-brief-template.md) DO rails 9 and 10) for the same two failure classes. ## 2026-06-27, Library Version 2026.06.369, PR #390

Audit-tooling hardening for local project: close a CCM/AICM catalogue-confusion hole in the compliance-matrix control-code gate (gate 49). The matrix's "CSA CCM v4.1" column was validated only by the corpus-wide CSA citation gate (gate 48), which checks a matrix token against the AICM-wins union and so would pass an AICM-only code (for example an `MDS-` Model Security code, an AICM v1.1 domain that CCM v4.1 does not have) sitting in a column labelled CCM v4.1. Gate 49 now validates that column for CCM v4.1.0 catalogue membership and flags an AICM-only identifier as a CCM/AICM confusion, complementary to gate 48 (which keeps CCM/AICM title accuracy). Splits the blended `VALID_DOMAINS` in [`tools/ccm_aicm_reference.py`](tools/ccm_aicm_reference.py) into per-catalogue `CCM_DOMAINS` (17) and `AICM_DOMAINS` (18) with `is_ccm_v41` / `is_aicm` / `is_aicm_only` helpers, so a caller can enforce catalogue discipline rather than relying on the union. Adds three regression fixtures (an AICM-only code, an unknown code, a valid-code false-positive guard) replacing the prior "CCM not policed here" test, and updates the audit-programme spec sections 5 and 6 gate-49 narrative. The crib and every code used were cross-validated against the scratch repo's `ref/standards/` source extracts (the in-repo CCM module matches the CSA CCM v4.1.0 catalogue CSV exactly at 207 codes; the NIST CSF module matches CSWP-29 at 22 categories). Also batches the clean **Sweep 60** `/validate` history row in [`.working/validate-sweeps/history.md`](.working/validate-sweeps/history.md) (the #389 loop-break compensating control over the #387/#388/#389 deltas; 0 findings across all three subagents; no asserted-expectations contradiction). ## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.354, PR #375

`.claude/` operating-procedure change for local project: codified the **wind-down decision framework** in [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) (a new section after the attended-autonomous operating mode). It converts the session-ending handoff from a silent unilateral call into a surfaced decision: whenever the assistant concludes a handoff is right, it presents its justification, a per-PR likelihood-of-success assessment of the pending next-five PRs (anchored to objective tractability signals, not a subjective read), and named options (A handoff / B recommended additional PRs / C higher-risk order / D a deliberate Ulysses-pact impulse-check that triggers an immediate handoff if chosen). The decision uses the same roughly-2-minute graceful-degradation timer as the attended-autonomous mechanism and defaults to handoff on no answer; Quality > Speed stays the tiebreaker and options B/C are bounded ("one more, re-assess, repeat", full per-PR `/validate-pr` + `/retro` each). Cross-referenced from the [`.working/session-handoff.md`](.working/session-handoff.md) standing-disciplines bullet. Also batches the PR #374 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) + `/retro` rows (the latter surfaced an update-one-of-a-pair pattern candidate). Maintainer-directed (the framework was this session's purpose, per the branch name). Library `2026.06.353` to `2026.06.354`; README `1.9.224` to `1.9.225`.

## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.349, PR #370

Integrity-tooling track (PR 1 of 3, the gate-49 extension / DD-12 migration): added [`tools/lint-document-control-codes.py`](tools/lint-document-control-codes.py), a corpus-wide sibling of gate 49 ([`tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py`](tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py)) that validates NIST CSF 2.0 control codes wherever they appear in any corpus document's framework-reference or crosswalk tables, not only the central compliance matrix. It reuses the authoritative 22-Category CSF 2.0 set and the CSF-1.1 relocation map in [`tools/nist_csf_reference.py`](tools/nist_csf_reference.py), recognises both the framework-as-row and framework-as-column table shapes, strips subcategory suffixes (`DE.CM-7` to `DE.CM`) and validates at the Category level, and is precision-first: it extracts codes only from the code cell of a framework-row (never trailing notes cells) and only from the NIST column of a column-table, so a CSF-1.1 code inside a legitimate rename note is not a false positive. Scoped to NIST CSF 2.0 (per-document ISO Annex A deferred to a follow-up); excludes the central matrix (gate 49's target) and the [`dev-security/claude-rules/`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md) pack subtree. The scanner is shipped as a discovery tool, not yet wired as an audit gate: run corpus-wide it reports the authoritative DD-12 carrier inventory (5 CSF-1.1-era codes across 3 files: [`risk/standard-third-party-and-supply-chain-risk.md`](risk/standard-third-party-and-supply-chain-risk.md):230 `ID.SC`; [`operations/procedure-security-monitoring-and-alert-management.md`](operations/procedure-security-monitoring-and-alert-management.md):333/336/337 `RS.RP`/`DE.DP`/`DE.DP`; [`compliance/procedure-capa.md`](compliance/procedure-capa.md):475 `RC.IM`), so wiring it as a gate now would fail until those carriers migrate (PR 2 of the track); the gate wiring lands in PR 3 once the corpus is clean. A `DocumentControlCodeTests` regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py) covers both table shapes, the subcategory-strip, the notes-cell precision guard, the NIST-SP-row non-match, and valid/unknown-category cases. Also batches the Sweep 54 loop-break `/validate` history row (the `/resume` compensating control for session-closing handoff PR #369, covering the #366/#367/#368/#369 deltas; full A/B/C dispatch, 0 findings clean, no asserted-expectations contradiction) and advances the TODO sweep cursor to Sweep 54. Library `2026.06.348` to `2026.06.349`; README `1.9.219` to `1.9.220`.

## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.347, PR #368

Integrity-tooling aid closing TODO §4.14 (CHANGELOG-hygiene first-commit pre-flight): added [`tools/preflight-changelog.py`](tools/preflight-changelog.py), a commit-gating helper run as `python3 tools/preflight-changelog.py && git commit ...` that exits non-zero when the *added* lines of the root [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md) or its detailed mirror carry an em-dash or en-dash in prose (code spans stripped first, matching gate 51) or a path-shaped backtick code span not wrapped in a markdown link (mirroring [`tools/lint-changelog-link-coverage.py`](tools/lint-changelog-link-coverage.py)). Scoped to added lines so historical entries never false-alarm. It is the durable commit-gating form the §4.14 escalation called for (a check that gates the commit, not one that merely reports alongside an unconditional `&& git commit`); a standalone helper rather than a pre-commit hook because no `.git/hooks/pre-commit` fires on commits in this environment (verified before building). Documented in a [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md) close-out-checklist bullet. It is a developer aid, not a new audit gate; the authoritative gates (D3, gate 51, link-coverage) remain in CI. ## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.345, PR #366

Integrity-tooling delta gate closing TODO §4.17 (the Version-Date co-bump check): added **delta gate D4 (per-PR Version-Date co-bump)**, [`tools/check-date-cobump-on-pr.py`](tools/check-date-cobump-on-pr.py), a PR-only check (sibling to D1/D2/D3) that fails when a PR bumps a versioned document's `**Version:**` field but leaves its `**Date:**` field not equal to the date of the bump commit (UTC). It closes the residue that gates 40 (corpus version-bump-recency) and 31 (document-date-staleness) leave open: gate 40 is silent on the Date, and gate 31 tolerates a 1-day lag, so a Version bump whose Date was left one day stale passes (the recurring sub-shape `/retro` confirmed at PR #325 and PR #352). It is delta-scoped rather than a HEAD-state gate-40 extension because prototyping showed a HEAD-state form has a roughly 78-document historical false-positive surface (a single 2026-05-31 mass commit accounts for dozens), whereas the delta form sees only the PR diff and so has none; comparing against the bump commit's date also keeps it false-positive-free for same-day sequential PRs. Wired into [`.github/workflows/quality.yml`](.github/workflows/quality.yml), the pre-push runner [`tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh`](tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh), and [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) §6.1 (`1.16.9` to `1.16.10`), with a `DateCobumpOnPrTests` regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py). Also batches the **Sweep 53** loop-break `/validate` history row and per-iteration detail file (the `/resume` compensating control for session-closing handoff PRs #363 and #365, covering the #362/#363/#364/#365 deltas; full A/B/C dispatch, 1 out-of-window note cross-referenced into DD-12, 0 in-window). Library `2026.06.344` to `2026.06.345`; audit-programme spec `1.16.9` to `1.16.10`; README `1.9.215` to `1.9.216`.

## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.341, PR #362

Integrity-tooling gate closing the TODO P2 directional-dependency gate: added **gate 53 (corpus-to-project directional-dependency)**, [`tools/lint-directional-dependency.py`](tools/lint-directional-dependency.py), the mechanical backstop for the project-governance-separation spec §4 one-way dependency rule. It flags any deliverable-corpus document that contains a markdown link whose resolved target is inside [`.project-governance/`](.project-governance/README.md) (a corpus-to-project link inverts the dependency; project governance depends on the corpus, never the reverse); it is the §4 counterpart to gate 52's §7.4 scan-scope parity, the two together making the separation spec's dependency invariants standing mechanical checks rather than migration-discipline conventions. The deliverable-corpus scan set is derived from [`tools/lint_common.py`](tools/lint_common.py) `AUDITED_DOMAIN_DIRS` minus `.project-governance` plus the root deliverable specifications, so a future audited domain propagates from one place and the gate does not itself hardcode the domain run gate 52 forbids; the non-deliverable surfaces §4 permits to link into the directory (the pack under [`dev-security/claude-rules/`](dev-security/claude-rules/README.md), the backlog [`TODO.md`](TODO.md), the root [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md), the generated indexes, the `.working/` and `.claude/` trees) are out of scope. Detection mirrors the broken-link checker (gate 3): fenced blocks and external targets are skipped, and a target is resolved relative to its source before the `.project-governance` path-component test, so every relative shape is caught. The corpus is clean on landing (no deliverable document links into the directory; the migration that created it severed every such link in PR #336). Wired into all four surfaces with a `DirectionalDependencyTests` regression class; the §7.3 narrative is rewritten from "queued" to built, and the §4 cross-reference updated. Also batches the **Sweep 52** loop-break `/validate` history row (the #361 compensating control over the #359/#360/#361 deltas, 0 findings clean). ## 2026-06-26, Library Version 2026.06.336, PR #357

Added **gate 51 (working-tree prose-hygiene)** to the audit programme: [`tools/lint-working-prose-hygiene.py`](tools/lint-working-prose-hygiene.py) forbids em-dashes and en-dashes in the prose of the `.working/` maintainer tree (the tree every other content linter exempts) while allowing them inside inline code spans and fenced code blocks, so the 2026-06-26 `.working/` em-dash conformance (#353) cannot silently regress. Wired into all four audit surfaces ([`tools/run_all_audits.sh`](tools/run_all_audits.sh), [`.github/workflows/quality.yml`](.github/workflows/quality.yml), [`.pre-commit-config.yaml`](.pre-commit-config.yaml), and [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) §6 as row 51) with a `WorkingProseHygieneTests` regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py); the gate-39-blind growth-narrative word-form in [`dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) bumped from "fifty" to "fifty-one". Implementation note: the inline-code-span stripper uses the standard CommonMark code-span regex (a run of N backticks, content, a closing run of N) rather than a naive single-backtick strip, which mis-pairs spans whose content contains backticks (the self-referential handoff line that quoted the design was exactly such a case, and was rephrased). Also batches the **Sweep 50** loop-break `/validate` history row (the deferred #354/#356 compensating control over the #352 to #356 deltas; 0 findings, corpus byte-identical to the Sweep-48/49 state). ## 2026-06-25, Library Version 2026.06.322, PR #343

**Gate 50 (Bookkeeping-parity audit) added to the audit programme** ([`tools/lint-bookkeeping-parity.py`](tools/lint-bookkeeping-parity.py)), the §4.11 worker-provenance / bookkeeping-parity gate family member. It is the honest mechanical backstop for the per-PR QA cadence and the backlog-to-DONE rotation discipline: it enforces the PRESENCE of the bookkeeping records the process mandates, not their semantic correctness. Check 1 (QA-cadence parity) derives the merged-PR list from the `## ... PR #N` headers in [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md) and, for each PR in `[INCEPTION=329, max(PR))`, requires a row in [`.working/validate-pr/history.md`](.working/validate-pr/history.md) and (for substantive PRs) [`.working/improvement-log.md`](.working/improvement-log.md), with the highest-PR batch-lag exemption, the session-closing-handoff-PR exemption (detected by the `SKIPPED`/`handoff-PR exception` Findings cell), the subsumption/maintainer-exception row (the #328 instance), and a `KNOWN_HANDOFF_NO_ROW` allowlist (`#300`/`#322`/`#334`) for handoff PRs merged before the exemption-row convention. Check 2 (TODO/DONE rotation parity) is precision-first / FP-free: it flags only unambiguous self-completion markers on a backlog bullet (uppercase `SHIPPED in #N`/`DONE in #N`, `Status: completed|done|shipped`, a `[done]`/`[shipped]`/`[x]` checkbox/suffix, or a leading strikethrough), with code-span and bullet-start precision so the open FR-167 batch-sequence strikethrough and the maintenance-note convention reference are not flagged. Check 3 (worker-provenance attestation) is a documented dormant stub until the worker-delivered marking convention and the external-collaborator primitive exist. Wired into all four audit surfaces (gate count **49 to 50**) with a 13-case regression class in [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py); modelled on gate 45 ([`tools/lint-todo-staleness.py`](tools/lint-todo-staleness.py)) and deliberately kept out of the pre-push history-aware runner (it parses committed content, not the commit graph, so [`tools/run_all_audits.sh`](tools/run_all_audits.sh) already covers it pre-push). Also corrects the [`dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/guardrail-review/SKILL.md) growth-narrative word-form "a dozen gates to forty-nine" to "fifty" (gate-39-blind, fixed proactively rather than left for the next sweep; pack `1.49.11` to `1.49.12`), and queues [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) §4.13 (a maintainer-requested `/guardrails` coherence review of the 50-gate inventory, maintainer-directed to run immediately upon the gate-50 addition). Batches the zero-finding **Sweep 47** `/validate` history row (the #342 loop-break compensating control, clean). [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) `1.16.5` to `1.16.6`; taxonomy and scorecard regenerated. ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.304, PR #325

Added **gate 49 (Matrix control-code validity audit)** to the audit programme: a new linter [`tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py`](tools/lint-matrix-control-codes.py) that validates the framework-control codes in [`compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md`](compliance/matrix-grc-compliance-alignment.md) for the columns no existing gate covers. It checks every ISO 27001:2022 column token is a real Annex A control code (`A.5`-`A.8` within each theme's count: 37/8/14/34, 93 total) or a management-system clause (`§4`-`§10`), and every NIST CSF 2.0 token is well-formed (`FUNCTION.CATEGORY` with a CSF 2.0 Core Function prefix). ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.303, PR #324

`.claude/` + `.working/` process codification for local project: codified the maintainer-accepted **handoff asserted-expectations** convention. A session-closing handoff now records, scoped to the surfaces it actually verified or covered with a formal QA pass, what it asserts clean (plus a `green-at-<sha>` mechanical-baseline line), and the next `/resume`'s corpus-wide `/validate` cross-checks its findings against those claims: a contradiction of a claimed-clean touched surface reads as a genuine miss rather than an ordinary out-of-window finding. This is the cheap loop-break signal that replaces a wasteful second close-time `/validate` (rejected because the corpus is byte-identical across the boundary, so two non-deterministic subagent runs would differ only by sampling variance; the one deterministic close-vs-start diff worth keeping is the mechanical `green-at-<sha>`, already re-checked at `/resume`). Surfaces: a new `## Asserted expectations` section + the `green-at-<sha>` line in [`.working/session-handoff.md`](.working/session-handoff.md); PR-workflow step 5c, the close-out checklist, and the two handoff mechanisms in [`.claude/CLAUDE.md`](.claude/CLAUDE.md); steps 3 and 5 of [`.claude/commands/resume.md`](.claude/commands/resume.md). ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.300, PR #321

**FR-140: resolve the adopter starter-set divergence.** The library presented four different "starter set" sizes across its adopter on-ramps (a 6-artefact Day-1 floor, a 15-document Tier 1 set, a ~25-document sector path, and a ~37-artefact README "Core reference set"), and, more substantively, the 6-artefact Day-1 floor named the acceptable-use and identity-and-access-management policies as non-negotiable while the *larger* 15-document Tier 1 set omitted both, so the floor was not a subset of Tier 1. Per maintainer decision (Option A), [`docs/adopter-guide.md`](docs/adopter-guide.md) Tier 1 gains [`security/policy-acceptable-use.md`](security/policy-acceptable-use.md) and [`security/policy-identity-and-access-management.md`](security/policy-identity-and-access-management.md) (15 → 17 documents), making the Day-1 floor a strict subset; the `15`→`17` count and the floor/Tier-1 reconciliation prose are harmonized across [`docs/template-quickstart.md`](docs/template-quickstart.md), [`docs/adopter-guide.md`](docs/adopter-guide.md), and [`docs/decision-tree.md`](docs/decision-tree.md); and [`README.md`](README.md)'s "Core reference set" is reframed as the curated foundational *catalogue* an adopter grows toward (cross-referenced to the quickstart/adopter-guide starting points) rather than a competing "authoritative starter set". To make the Day-1 floor a strict subset of the catalogue too, the README core reference set gains the two floor artefacts it was missing, [`security/policy-acceptable-use.md`](security/policy-acceptable-use.md) and [`security/procedure-security-incident-response.md`](security/procedure-security-incident-response.md) (it already carried the other four). Closes FR-140. Also bundles, per recursion-avoidance, the #320 `/validate-pr` + `/retro` register rows and the one out-of-window finding that sweep surfaced: [`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md):133's "2026 Update summary" said Bill C-27 "Remained under parliamentary study as of early 2026", corrected to the corpus consensus (lapsed at the 2025-01-06 prorogation; PIPEDA in force). Taxonomy and scorecard regenerated. Library `2026.06.298` to `2026.06.300`; README `1.9.169` to `1.9.171`. ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.298, PR #320

**DD-8: scrub the live-regime sense of CPPA to PIPEDA across the corpus.** The Consumer Privacy Protection Act (CPPA, Part 1 of Canada's Bill C-27) never became law (the bill lapsed at the 2025-01-06 prorogation); PIPEDA remains the in-force Canadian federal private-sector privacy regime. This sweep corrects the corpus's residual treatment of CPPA as a current/applicable regime, a **full principled scrub** (maintainer-chosen) across **29 documents**: bare `CPPA` in a live-applicable framework list became `PIPEDA` (e.g. [`security/procedure-security-incident-response.md`](security/procedure-security-incident-response.md) §6 notification table + §6.2 heading, [`risk/standard-enterprise-risk-management.md`](risk/standard-enterprise-risk-management.md), [`security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md`](security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md), [`supply-chain/procedure-supplier-due-diligence.md`](supply-chain/procedure-supplier-due-diligence.md)); `PIPEDA / CPPA` pairs dropped the redundant live-CPPA (the sector annexes, [`privacy/register-cross-border-data-flow.md`](privacy/register-cross-border-data-flow.md), [`privacy/template-joint-controller-arrangement.md`](privacy/template-joint-controller-arrangement.md)); the three [`governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md`](governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md) Frameworks tags for the docs PR #264 already body-scrubbed were reconciled to PIPEDA; CPPA-specific content was qualified rather than replaced ([`risk/annex-ai-risk-methodology.md`](risk/annex-ai-risk-methodology.md) algorithmic-transparency row to `CPPA (Canada, proposed)`; [`privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md`](privacy/annex-privacy-jurisdiction-index.md) coverage row to `CPPA (pending)`); and a factual error in [`governance/register-glossary.md`](governance/register-glossary.md) ("PIPEDA being superseded by CPPA") was fixed. **Preserved**: the distinct California Privacy Protection Agency (CPPA) sense in [`privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-united-states.md`](privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-united-states.md), and every mention already qualified pending/proposed/lapsed (the Canada annex, the privacy crosswalk rows, [`governance/register-canonical-citations.md`](governance/register-canonical-citations.md)). Closes DD-8 (surfaced by PR #264 / FR-138, which deferred the broader sweep). Also carries the `/resume` corpus-wide **Sweep 40** history row and detail file ([`.working/validate-sweeps/2026-06-24-sweep40-iter1.md`](.working/validate-sweeps/2026-06-24-sweep40-iter1.md)): 1 in-window note on [`dev-security/claude-rules/languages/go.md`](dev-security/claude-rules/languages/go.md) TLS-field precision (`PreferServerCipherSuites` is deprecated and ignored in current Go, not "TLS 1.2 and below" as the #318 comment grouped it), which the maintainer chose to **fold into this PR** rather than defer: the comment is reworded so `CipherSuites` (TLS-1.2-scoped) and `PreferServerCipherSuites` (deprecated/ignored) are described distinctly; the #318 load-bearing TLS-1.3 claim is unchanged. ## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.292, PR #314

**New [`governance/specification-project-governance-separation.md`](governance/specification-project-governance-separation.md): a process separating corpus/library governance from project governance.** Adds a Specification (v1.0.1) drawing the boundary between the governance content the library publishes as its deliverable (corpus/library governance) and the operational records of running this project (project governance), which had both accumulated in `governance/`. The criterion is reusable-pattern-versus-operational-instance: a specification, procedure, or template of a process is a reusable pattern (corpus); the filled-in record of having executed that process on this corpus is an operational instance (project). The boundary is kept clean by a one-way dependency rule (project governance may cite corpus; corpus must not cite project governance), which makes the corpus document index corpus-only and turns any migration into citation surgery rather than a file move. Project-governance artefacts will live in a new top-level `.project-governance/` directory (dot-prefixed like `.working/` and `.claude/`, but NOT exempt: fully audited, with adopter-facing generator and index inclusion the only sweep behaviour that changes). The spec classifies all 40 current `governance/` artefacts (§5): 33 stay corpus (including this spec and, by maintainer decision 2026-06-24, [`register-canonical-citations.md`](governance/register-canonical-citations.md) as the reusable citation reference whose verification log is the operational instance), 6 (the citation-verification campaign cluster) migrate in Phase 1, and 2 ([`register-coverage-gaps.md`](governance/register-coverage-gaps.md), [`register-document-review-schedule.md`](governance/register-document-review-schedule.md)) are deferred to per-artefact later decisions. This closes the deferred backlog item R2 by principle (the citation-verification cluster is project governance, so it migrates in Phase 1) and records why R1 was correctly closed won't-move (scanner-private config already in [`tools/`](tools/)). No files move in this PR; Phase 1 migration, the queued directional-dependency gate (§7.3), and the deferred classifications are queued in [`TODO.md`](TODO.md). Wired into [`governance/README.md`](governance/README.md) and the corpus document index; taxonomy, portal, and scorecard regenerated. Carries the batched #313 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.291` to `2026.06.292`; README `1.9.162` to `1.9.163`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.287, PR #309

**S5: gate 48 (CSA CCM/AICM citation-accuracy) gains a bare-domain-code check (Check 4).** Closes the TODO S5 item (surfaced by Sweep 36, where PR #298's reconciliation left bare domain-code residuals that the token-scoped gate could not see and the orchestrator grep had to catch). [`tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py`](tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py) now flags a bare superseded or fabricated CCM domain code (one with no `<DOMAIN>-<NN>` suffix, in a framework family list, a domain-keyed crosswalk row, or a glossary-style entry) when the line either names the matrices (CCM / CSA / Cloud Controls Matrix / AICM) or sits under a CCM/AICM section heading, and is not a historical rename-note. The design is precision-first: the token boundary excludes `.NET`, the corpus-internal `AI-GOV` / `MODEL-GOV` identifiers, and the `<CODE>-<NN>` control tokens; the CCM-context requirement excludes currency `AUD` and "government" prose; a rename-note exemption (`renamed` / `superseded` / `corrected` and similar) clears the glossary I&S rename-note and the pack-README version-history rows; and [`TODO.md`](TODO.md) is added to the gate's meta-exempt set (it names the codes when describing the gate's own follow-up items). The recall limit is documented: a bad code in a multi-framework mapping table where the CCM column is unlabelled on the row and the section heading is generic is not caught (the apply-time grep and the periodic sweep cover that tail). Four regression cases added to [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py) (two fire cases for the family-list and CCM-section shapes, two false-positive guards for the rename-note and the `.NET`/currency cases); gate 48 stays clean on the corpus (376 files; TODO now exempt). Still 48 gates, no parity change; completes the gate-48 enhancement pair with S4 (#308). Carries the batched #308 `/validate-pr` (0 in-window findings, 1 self-resolved out-of-window note) and `/retro` records. Library `2026.06.286` to `2026.06.287`; README `1.9.157` to `1.9.158`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-24, Library Version 2026.06.286, PR #308

**S4: gate 48 (CSA CCM/AICM citation-accuracy) gains a section-aware, cross-catalogue title check.** Closes the TODO S4 item (surfaced by PR #299's `/validate-pr`). [`tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py`](tools/lint-ccm-aicm-citations.py)'s control-listing title check is now **section-aware**: a row under a `## CSA CCM ...` heading is checked against the CCM v4.1.0 title, one under an `## AICM ...` heading against the AICM v1.1.0 title, and one under neither against the AICM-wins union (the prior behaviour, preserved for unscoped tables). A new **cross-catalogue check** flags the gate-escaping class the union check is blind to: a small set of controls share a code across both matrices but carry titles differing by a distinctive content word (I&S-07 is "Migration to Cloud Environments" in CCM v4.1.0 but "Migration to Hosted Environments" in AICM v1.1.0), and because the two titles share most content words the conservative content-word check never fires on the mix-up. The new check fails a row under a CCM section that carries the AICM variant's distinctive word (and none of the CCM variant's), and vice versa; this is exactly the I&S-07 confusion that PR #299's `/validate-pr` had to catch by hand. Controls differing only by punctuation (IAM-11's "Customers" vs "Customers'") have no distinctive content word and are intentionally not policed, consistent with the gate's tolerance of localized wording. Two regression cases added to [`tests/test_linters.py`](tests/test_linters.py) (the cross-catalogue fail case plus a false-positive guard for the correct title); gate 48 stays clean on the corpus (still 48 gates, no parity change, an enhancement to the existing gate). Carries the batched #307 `/validate-pr` (0 findings, clean) and `/retro` records. Library `2026.06.285` to `2026.06.286`; README `1.9.156` to `1.9.157`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.256, PR #278

**DD-1: add PR-time delta gate D3 so new CHANGELOG entries follow the no-dash prose convention, leaving history untouched.** Deferred decision DD-1 asked whether to bring the root [`CHANGELOG.md`](CHANGELOG.md) under the em-dash and en-dash prohibition that [`tools/lint-language.py`](tools/lint-language.py) enforces on the corpus. The CHANGELOG sits outside that whole-file linter because its append-only history holds roughly 130 dashes accumulated before the convention applied, and rewriting historical entries would churn the record and risk altering past entries' meaning. The maintainer chose the new-entries-only resolution: a PR-time delta gate (D3, [`tools/check-changelog-dash-on-pr.py`](tools/check-changelog-dash-on-pr.py)) that inspects only the CHANGELOG lines a PR adds and fails on any em dash or en dash, so future entries follow the convention while history stays intact. Wired into the local PR-time runner [`tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh`](tools/run-pr-time-checks.sh), CI ([`.github/workflows/quality.yml`](.github/workflows/quality.yml), PR-only, alongside D1 and D2), and the audit-programme spec [`governance/specification-audit-programme.md`](governance/specification-audit-programme.md) section 6.1 (`1.15.0 → 1.16.0`). The scope was re-confirmed with the maintainer at action time after investigation found roughly 130 dashes (not the approximately five the decision assumed), making a whole-file rewrite disproportionate. Also carries the batched PR #277 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) and `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.255 → 2026.06.256`; README `1.9.126 → 1.9.127`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.250, PR #272

**FR-166: corpus listing-surface completeness gate + authoring-time sweep tool.** Governance work must be meticulous, so when a new document is added, every surface that should list it must be updated. This PR adds the mechanism. The new **gate 47** ([`tools/lint-listing-surface-completeness.py`](tools/lint-listing-surface-completeness.py)) enforces completeness for the MECHANICAL listing surfaces against the canonical active-document set in [`taxonomy.yml`](taxonomy.yml): the document-index register ([`governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md`](governance/register-document-index-and-classification.md)) must list every domain-prefixed active document, and each domain README must reference every active document in its own domain. Root-level meta-specifications (`specification-*.md`) are exempt by a documented rule (the register is organized by domain and has never indexed them). The new authoring helper [`tools/suggest-listing-surfaces.py`](tools/suggest-listing-surfaces.py) `<doc>` reports, for a new document, the MECHANICAL surfaces (present/missing) plus a ranked high-recall list of SEMANTIC candidates (the framework matrices and crosswalks, the glossary, the Related Documents field) for a human to ratify. Honest contract per `gate-discipline`: MECHANICAL surfaces are hard-gated; the relevance-based SEMANTIC surfaces are NOT gated (a noisy completeness gate over a judgment-based surface would erode gate-discipline), they get suggestions and a `/validate` Subagent B coverage-drift check instead. Wired across all four audit-programme surfaces (workflow, runner, pre-commit, spec §6) with a regression fixture; the gate count moves 46 → 47. The corpus is already complete (the gate passes at HEAD); the only register gap measured (the two root meta-specs) is the documented exemption. Also wires the helper into the new-document procedure ([`specification-ingestion.md`](specification-ingestion.md) checklist item 12) and adds the SEMANTIC coverage-drift check to the [`validation-sweep`](dev-security/claude-rules/skills/validation-sweep/SKILL.md) SKILL's Subagent B scope. Carries the batched PR #271 `/validate-pr` (0 findings) + `/retro` rows. Per-doc: audit-programme spec `1.14.2 → 1.15.0`, ingestion spec `1.7.2 → 1.7.3`; pack `1.49.2 → 1.49.3`; library `2026.06.249 → 2026.06.250`; README `1.9.120 → 1.9.121`. See [`.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md`](.working/changelog-details/CHANGELOG-detailed.md) for detail.

## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.249, PR #271

**Sweep 28 (`/validate`) close-out: fix an in-window DR backup-cadence contradiction surfaced by the session-resume sweep.** The `/resume` compensating-control corpus-wide `/validate` (the standing control for the session-closing handoff PR #270, which skips its trailing `/validate-pr`) ran a full three-subagent dispatch over the whole corpus + the #259-#270 window. FR-139 fixed Tier 1's cadence but, in rewriting the gap clause to bind Tier 2 explicitly to 4 hours, left Tier 2 on the old "daily" cadence. Fixed here: the cadence clause now reads "backups at least every 4 hours for Tier 2's 4-hour RPO, and at least daily backups for Tier 3 and Tier 4" — consistent with the gap clause, the RTO/RPO targets table, and the locked FR-139 principle (cadence must meet RPO), so no new authorial decision (the binding 4-hour gap requirement was already present at :99); per-doc version `1.3.0 → 1.3.1`. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.245, PR #267

**FR-141 (High): remove the invented PIPEDA breach "72-hour target".** Canada's federal `PIPEDA` Breach of Security Safeguards Regulations require reporting to the OPC "as soon as feasible after the organization determines that the breach has occurred" — there is no fixed statutory hour clock, so the "(72-hour target)" annotation was a fabricated deadline (the 72-hour figure is GDPR's, and Quebec Law 25's to the CAI — neither is the PIPEDA federal rule). A bare-token search found the invented annotation at two surfaces (not just the one named in the finding): [`privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md`](privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md):171 (`1.4.9 → 1.4.10`; §6.2 jurisdiction table, "Without unreasonable delay (72-hour target)") and [`security/procedure-security-incident-response.md`](security/procedure-security-incident-response.md):176 (`1.3.8 → 1.3.9`; §6 regulatory-notification table, "As soon as feasible (72-hour target)"). Both deadline cells now read "As soon as feasible (no fixed statutory deadline)". The correct 72-hour references elsewhere (GDPR threshold in [`risk/template-risk-appetite-statement.md`](risk/template-risk-appetite-statement.md), Quebec Law 25 to the CAI, Malaysia's PDPC rule) were verified accurate and left unchanged. That §176 cell's separate "CPPA (Canada)" regime label (an FR-138 CPPA-not-in-force issue) is left for the deferred broader-CPPA sweep (logged in [`.working/overnight-pr.md`](.working/overnight-pr.md)); only the FR-141 deadline was changed here. Carries the batched PR #266 `/validate-pr` (0 in-window) + `/retro` rows. Library `2026.06.244 → 2026.06.245`; README `1.9.115 → 1.9.116`. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.243, PR #265

**FR-139 (H[critical]): DR Tier-1 backup cadence aligned to the 1-hour RPO.** [`resilience/plan-it-disaster-recovery.md`](resilience/plan-it-disaster-recovery.md) set a 1-hour RPO for Tier 1 (Mission Critical) in its RTO/RPO targets table, but the backup section mandated "automated daily backups" and a "backup gap not exceeding 24 hours for Tier 1" — both incompatible with a 1-hour RPO. Combined with the rule that "any backup gap exceeding the defined RPO is treated as a P2 risk event", a compliant Tier-1 system would *permanently* sit in P2 escalation, a self-contradiction. Per the maintainer's locked decision (1h RPO binding; the 24h figure is the error and belongs to lower tiers), the backup cadence now requires continuous or near-continuous data protection (journaled/snapshot replication or log shipping) for Tier 1's 1-hour RPO with at least daily backups for Tier 2 and below, and the backup-gap limit is stated per tier (1 hour Tier 1, 4 hours Tier 2; 24h/72h for Tier 3/Tier 4 per the targets table). Per-doc version `1.2.0 → 1.3.0` (minor; the Tier-1 backup-cadence requirement changed substantively). A bare-token search confirms the DR plan is now internally consistent and that [`operations/standard-production-security-requirements.md`](operations/standard-production-security-requirements.md):43 ("RPO 1 hour, RTO 4 hours") corroborates rather than diverges. **This completes the six-item H[critical] locked-criticals batch (FR-134 through FR-139).** Carries the batched PR #264 `/validate-pr` (0 in-window) + `/retro` rows. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.242, PR #264

**FR-138 (H[critical]): scrub CPPA-as-live from the three named privacy documents.** The Consumer Privacy Protection Act (CPPA, Part 1 of Bill C-27) lapsed at the 2025-01-06 prorogation and is not in force ([`privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-canada.md`](privacy/jurisdictions/annex-privacy-canada.md):28 is the canonical statement; PIPEDA remains the federal private-sector law), yet three documents cited CPPA as a live legal basis — with invented-looking section numbers ("CPPA s.63", "s.66", "s.69", "s.67", "s.63(3)") presented as current obligations. Per the maintainer's locked decision, those are replaced with the in-force PIPEDA Schedule 1 basis (the CSA Model Code fair-information principles), with a "CPPA pending reintroduction" note where relevant. [`privacy/procedure-data-subject-rights-management.md`](privacy/procedure-data-subject-rights-management.md) (`1.4.1 → 1.5.0`): the rights table and the summary mapping table now cite PIPEDA Schedule 1 Principle 9 (Individual Access) for access/correction and Principle 3 (Consent, withdrawal) for objection; the erasure and automated-decision rows drop the CPPA citation because PIPEDA provides no such right (GDPR remains the basis); a new "Canadian legal basis" note explains this and that CPPA, if reintroduced, would add disposal and automated-decision rights; the intro, the §4 alignment line, the fees-table row, and the §8.3 heading are de-CPPA'd. [`privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md`](privacy/procedure-data-protection-and-privacy-breach-response.md) (`1.4.8 → 1.4.9`): the Canada federal breach basis becomes PIPEDA (Breach of Security Safeguards Regulations) with "CPPA pending reintroduction"; the alignment line and the §notification-basis row aligned. **FR-136 (H[critical]): the data-retention schedule is authoritative for log retention.** The logging standard flatly required "a minimum of seven years" for security and audit logs ([`security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md`](security/standard-logging-and-monitoring.md):92), while the authoritative [`governance/register-data-retention-schedule.md`](governance/register-data-retention-schedule.md) tiers retention by log class (access logs 1 year, privileged-access session logs 2 years, SIEM events 1 year hot + 2 years cold, security incident records 5 years) and the records standard's IT/Security row said "1 to 3 years" — three different answers for the same logs. ## 2026-06-23, Library Version 2026.06.238, PR #260

**FR-134 (H[critical]): one canonical risk-scoring scale across the three risk documents.** The risk standard's §5.2 scoring scale diverged from the canonical risk-assessment procedure: the standard used likelihood labels Rare→Almost Certain and score-to-rating bands `1-5 / 6-10 / 11-15 / 16-25`, while [`risk/procedure-risk-assessment-methodology.md`](risk/procedure-risk-assessment-methodology.md) (the canonical methodology, per maintainer decision) uses Very Low→Very High and bands `1-4 / 5-9 / 10-16 / 17-25`, so the same risk score produced a different rating, review cadence, and escalation depending on which document an assessor read (e.g. a score of 16 was "Critical" under the standard but "High" under the procedure). [`risk/template-enterprise-risk-register.md`](risk/template-enterprise-risk-register.md) (whose bands already agreed and which already cited the procedure) has its stale likelihood labels fixed: the Inherent/Residual Likelihood fields and the 5×5 matrix axis move from Rare→Almost Certain to Very Low→Very High.
